Title: MR-CCC: Bayesian Mendelian Randomization for Causal Cell--Cell Communication

URL Source: https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.23917v1

Published Time: Tue, 28 Apr 2026 01:19:51 GMT

Number of Pages: 149

Markdown Content:
# MR-CCC: Bayesian Mendelian Randomization for Causal CellŌĆōCell Communication 

Bitan Sarkar 1 and Yang Ni 2ŌłŚ

1Department of Statistics, Texas A&M University, College Station, TX, USA 

2Department of Statistics and Data Sciences, The University of Texas at Austin, Austin, TX, USA 

Abstract 

CellŌĆōcell communication (CCC) is commonly inferred from ligandŌĆōreceptor co-expression, an associational paradigm that cannot distinguish causal signaling from shared regulation or confounding. We propose MR-CCC , a Bayesian Mendelian ran-domization framework that uses cis-eQTLs as instruments for ligand and receptor expression and explicitly models receptor-modulated ligand effects through an interac-tion term, so the causal effect of a ligand can vary with receptor abundance. A spikeŌĆō andŌĆōslab prior yields posterior inclusion probabilities quantifying evidence for causal signaling, and an efficient Gibbs sampler provides scalable inference. Benchmarked against naive regression, MVMR, and MR-BMA, MR-CCC controls false discoveries under confounding while retaining high power, and uniquely estimates both the lig-and main and receptor-modulated interaction effects. Applied to the OneK1K NK cells ŌåÆ monocytes axis, MR-CCC identifies eight discoveries across GABA, interferon, interleukin, and prostaglandin signaling, including a stoichiometry-dependent dissocia-tion of the two IL-18 receptor chains and co-discovery of both obligate IFN-╬│ receptor subunits. 

> ŌłŚ

Corresponding author: Yang Ni (yang.ni@austin.utexas.edu). 

1

> arXiv:2604.23917v1 [stat.ME] 27 Apr 2026

## 1 Introduction 

CellŌĆōcell communication (CCC) is a fundamental organizing principle of multicellular sys-tems, governing immune regulation, development, and disease progression. At the molecular level, CCC is mediated through ligandŌĆōreceptor interactions, whereby ligands expressed in a sender cell type bind cognate receptors in a receiver cell type to initiate downstream sig-naling programs. Advances in sequencing technologies have enabled large-scale mapping of these interactions across diverse biological systems, giving rise to computational frameworks such as CellPhoneDB 1 and CellChat 2.These methods have established a widely used paradigm for CCC inference based on co-expression and enrichment of ligandŌĆōreceptor pairs. However, this paradigm is funda-mentally associational: it identifies coordinated expression patterns but does not distinguish causal signaling from shared regulation or confounding. Ligand expression, receptor ex-pression, and downstream pathway activity may be jointly driven by latent factors such as donor heterogeneity, environmental exposures, or cell-state programs, leading to spurious communication signals. As a result, current CCC analyses can overestimate or misattribute intercellular signaling relationships. This limitation motivates a paradigm shift: rather than asking whether ligand and recep-tor expression are jointly elevated across cell types, the key causal question is instead whether 

variation in ligand expression in the sender cell type mechanically drives downstream path-way activity in the receiver cell type through receptor engagement, independently of any shared confounders. Mendelian randomization (MR) provides a principled strategy for pre-cisely this causal question by leveraging genetic variants as instrumental variables 3. Because germline variants are fixed at conception, they are largely independent of environmental and downstream confounders, enabling identification of causal effects under standard MR assumptions. MR has been widely applied in epidemiology and extended to settings with pleiotropy 4, multivariable exposures 5, and Bayesian formulations 6. However, existing MR approaches are not designed for CCC problems: they typically do not account for interac-tion effects, which are crucial for modeling receptor-modulated communication. In CCC, the effect of a ligand is inherently context-dependent and often modulated by receptor abun-2dance in the receiving cell. Capturing this interaction effect requires moving beyond additive models toward interaction-based causal formulations. At the same time, the large number of candidate ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway combinations necessitates principled selection proce-dures that can separate true communication signals from noise. To address these challenges, we introduce MR-CCC , a Bayesian Mendelian randomization framework for causal cellŌĆōcell communication inference. MR-CCC operationalizes this causal paradigm by jointly modeling ligand expression in the sender cell type, receptor expression in the receiver cell type, and downstream pathway activity within a coherent causal framework. The method uses cis-eQTLs as instruments for both ligand and receptor expression, replac-ing observed molecular quantities with their instrument-based conditional expectations to mitigate confounding. It explicitly incorporates receptor-modulated ligand effects through an interaction term, allowing communication strength to vary with receptor abundance. An identification result establishes that the plug-in working model recovers the structural causal coefficients under standard MR assumptions, even in the presence of the endogenous interaction term (Proposition 1). A spikeŌĆōandŌĆōslab prior enables probabilistic selection of communication effects, yielding posterior inclusion probabilities (PIPs) that quantify evi-dence for causal signaling. Posterior inference is carried out via an efficient Gibbs sampler with closed-form full conditionals for all model parameters, making MR-CCC computation-ally tractable for genome-scale CCC screens involving thousands of ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets. An overview of the framework, the simulation benchmark, and the lead biological discovery is shown in Figure 1. We benchmark MR-CCC against three alternatives ŌĆö naive regression (OLS), multivari-able Mendelian randomization (MVMR 5), and Bayesian model averaging MR (MR-BMA 6)ŌĆö across a null and two signal scenarios. MR-CCC alone combines strong null calibration, robustness to unmeasured confounding, and joint regularized estimation of both the ligand main and receptor-modulated interaction effects under a biologically motivated structural model. Applied to the OneK1K cohort 7 along the NK cells ŌåÆ monocytes axis, MR-CCC identifies eight high-confidence causal communication signals across GABA, interferon, interleukin, 3and prostaglandin signaling ŌĆö including a receptor stoichiometry-dependent dissociation of the two obligate IL-18 receptor chains ŌĆö while correctly assigning near-zero posterior probability to ICAM adhesion pairs and the reversed IL-15 direction, demonstrating senderŌĆō receiver-specific causal inference not achievable by co-expression tools. 

## 2 Results 

We evaluate MR-CCC in two complementary settings: simulation experiments that bench-mark its statistical properties against three alternatives, and an application to the OneK1K single-cell eQTL cohort. 

2.1 Simulation Study 

We conducted simulation experiments to evaluate MR-CCC. The study was designed to as-sess three aspects of performance: (i) discrimination between the absence and presence of CCC, (ii) estimation accuracy for the ligand main effect ╬▓X and the ligandŌĆōreceptor inter-action effect ╬▓XZ , and (iii) comparative performance relative to a naive regression baseline and two established MR alternatives. We simulated data from the model in Equation (1) at four sample sizes n Ōłł { 500 , 1000 , 10 ,000 , 30 ,000 } across three scenarios; full simulation parameter values are in Methods (Section 4.3). 

2.1.1 Simulation Scenarios 

Three scenarios were defined by the values of ╬▓X , ╬▓XZ , and ╬│ = 1 ŌłÆ I(╬▓X = ╬▓XZ = 0). 

Scenario 1 (S1): No communication, ╬│ = 0 , ╬▓X = 0 , ╬▓XZ = 0 . A null setting with neither a ligand main effect nor a ligand-receptor interaction. 

Scenario 2 (S2): Communication with receptor modulation, ╬│ = 1 , ╬▓X = 0 .3, ╬▓XZ =0.3. Communication is driven jointly by a ligand main effect and a receptor-modulated ligand effect. 4Scenario 3 (S3): Communication without receptor modulation, ╬│ = 1 , ╬▓X = 0 .3,

╬▓XZ = 0 . Communication is driven solely by the ligand main effect. 

2.1.2 Competing Methods 

We compared MR-CCC against three alternatives: ordinary least squares (OLS, naive regres-sion), multivariable Mendelian randomization (MVMR 5), and Bayesian model averaging MR (MR-BMA 6). Detailed implementations and decision rules for each method are in Methods (Sections 4.4 and 4.5). 

2.1.3 Simulation Results Scenario 1: No communication ( ╬│ = 0 , ╬▓X = 0 , ╬▓XZ = 0 )

Scenario 1 evaluates false positive behavior. A well-calibrated method should assign com-munication scores near zero, maintain negligible rejection rates, and recover both ╬▓X and 

╬▓XZ near zero. As shown in Table 1, MR-CCC satisfies all three criteria across all sample sizes. Its communication score ranges from 0.078ŌĆō0.130 across sample sizes, and its rejection rate is at most 5%. Both Bias( ╬▓X ) and MAD( ╬▓X ) shrink toward zero as n increases, reaching 0.001 (0.002) at n = 30 ,000; the same pattern holds for ╬▓XZ .The contrast with OLS is stark. OLS assigns a score of 1.000 and rejects in every single replicate at every sample size. Because X, Z, and Y share the unmeasured confounder U ,confounding alone generates an association signal indistinguishable from true communication under an associational model. Crucially, OLS does not self-correct as n grows: its bias in 

╬▓X remains at or above 0.151 even at n = 30 ,000, confirming that large sample sizes cannot rescue an associational paradigm under unmeasured confounding. MVMR substantially corrects the estimation bias by instrumenting both exposures, demonstrating the value of a causal CCC framework. Nevertheless, at the detection level MVMR does not fully resolve the false discovery problem: its null communication scores remain in the range 0.371ŌĆō0.564 and its rejection rate reaches 5% at n = 500. This re-flects residual finite-sample correlation between the instrumented ligand exposure ╦åX and 5the outcome even under the null. MR-BMA correctly identifies the absence of a ligand effect: its MIP X scores remain in the narrow range 0.040ŌĆō0.056 because the ligand instruments G do not predict Y after accounting for the receptor instruments H, which reflect the genuine receptor main effect 

╬▓Z = 0 .5. However, MR-BMA does not model ╬▓XZ , limiting its applicability when receptor-modulated communication is of scientific interest. MR-CCCŌĆÖs spikeŌĆōandŌĆōslab prior provides the additional regularization that closes this gap: by shrinking the communication effect vector toward zero unless the data supply suffi-ciently strong evidence of a signal, it controls false discoveries in a way that neither OLS nor MVMR achieves, while simultaneously producing a structured joint estimate of ( ╬▓X , ╬▓ XZ )that neither MR-BMA nor MVMR can provide. As shown in Figure 2, MR-CCC scores cluster tightly near zero, MR-BMA scores remain low, OLS scores sit uniformly at one, and MVMR occupies an intermediate range. 

Scenario 2: Communication with receptor modulation ( ╬│ = 1 , ╬▓X = 0 .3, ╬▓XZ = 0 .3)

Scenario 2 evaluates detection power when both the ligand main effect and the receptor-modulated interaction are present. A well-performing method should assign high communi-cation scores and reject in nearly all replicates. Table 2 shows that MR-CCC achieves this goal throughout. Its score reaches 0.996 already at n = 500 and is exactly 1.000 at larger sample sizes; its rejection rate is 1.000 at all n. More importantly, MR-CCC provides accurate joint estimation: Bias( ╬▓X ) = ŌłÆ0.003 and Bias( ╬▓XZ ) = 0 .006 at n = 500, converging toward zero with increasing n. OLS also rejects in every replicate, but its ╬▓X bias remains above 0.147 uniformly. MVMR matches MR-CCC in detection power; its score is 0.997 at n = 500 and exactly 1.000 at all larger sample sizes, a consequence of the frequentist null being severely violated by both causal signals. Its estimates of ╬▓X are accurate (bias near zero, MAD comparable to MR-CCC), confirming that MR correction resolves the confounding component; ╬▓XZ is not estimated by MVMR. This underperformance arises because MR-BMA operates on per-instrument summary statistics averaged across the interaction signal; when both ╬▓X and ╬▓XZ are nonzero, the reduced-form association of each instrument with 

Y conflates the two effects, making it harder for the BMA step to assign high posterior probability to the ligand model at small n. Furthermore, even at large sample sizes, MR-BMAŌĆÖs MACE for ╬▓X incurs a persistent negative bias (e.g. ŌłÆ0.028 at n = 30 ,000); this is a structural artifact of pooling all instrument information without explicitly modelling the interaction, so that part of the ligand effect is absorbed into the receptor-model term. MR-BMA provides no estimate of ╬▓XZ .7MR-CCCŌĆÖs combination of Bayesian regularization and explicit interaction modelling allows it to maintain full detection power at small n while providing reliable estimation of the full effect vector at all sample sizes. Figure 3 makes clear that OLS estimates are shifted uniformly upward, whereas MR-CCC and MVMR track the true value; Figure 4 shows that MR-CCC centers near the true ╬▓XZ = 0 .3; MVMR and MR-BMA are excluded from this figure as they do not model the interaction. In this scenario, communication is present ( ╬▓X╠Ė = 0) but the interaction is absent ( ╬▓XZ = 0). Table 3 shows that MR-CCC, MVMR, and MR-BMA all assign scores close to one and reject in nearly all replicates, correctly identifying the presence of communication. The more informative comparison comes from estimation accuracy. For ╬▓X , MR-CCC and MVMR both achieve small bias and decreasing MAD with n (MR-CCC: bias = 0 .017, MAD = 0 .047 at 

n = 500; bias = 0 .000, MAD = 0 .007 at n = 30 ,000). OLS again shows persistent upward bias exceeding 0.151 at all sample sizes, whereas MR-BMA incurs a small but persistent bias (e.g. ŌłÆ0.029 at n = 30 ,000) and provides no estimate of ╬▓XZ .The critical evaluation concerns ╬▓XZ , which is truly zero. Figure 4 shows that MR-CCC keeps estimates of ╬▓XZ tightly centered near zero across all sample sizes, with variability decreasing as n grows (MAD = 0 .036 at n = 500; MAD = 0 .004 at n = 30 ,000). In particular, the MR-CCC spikeŌĆōandŌĆōslab prior does not spuriously activate the interaction component when only the main effect is present. In summary, Scenario 3 confirms that MR-CCCŌĆÖs joint modelling of ( ╬▓X , ╬▓ XZ ) is not only powerful but also specific: it correctly infers the pattern of communication without inventing interaction effects that are not present in the data. 

Summary. MR-CCC uniquely combines strong null calibration, robustness to unmeasured confounding via Bayesian MR, and joint estimation of ( ╬▓X , ╬▓ XZ ) under a biologically moti-vated ligandŌĆōreceptor model. The real-data analysis below uses n = 651, which lies in the range where MR-CCCŌĆÖs advantage over competing methods is largest.

Donor-level expression con-struction, filtering, ligandŌĆōreceptor and pathway annotations, pathway-activity construction, and instrument selection are described in Methods (Section 4.6); after filtering, the analysis retained n = 651 donors and 41 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets spanning 11 biological pathways. 10 2.2.1 Results for NK Cells ŌåÆ Monocytes 

For each of the 41 triplets, MR-CCC was fitted using the Gibbs sampler with 20,000 itera-tions, a 2,000-iteration burn-in, and a thinning factor of 10. Posterior means of ╬▓X , ╬▓XZ , and 

╬▓Z were recorded together with the posterior inclusion probability PIP = Pr( ╬│ = 1 | data). All reported effect sizes are standardized: ╦å╬▓(s)

These span four biochemically distinct pathway classes ŌĆö interleukin, prostaglandin, GABA, and interferon signaling ŌĆö revealing a cytokine- and lipid-mediator-driven NKŌĆōmonocyte axis operating through soluble ligands rather than cell-contact adhesion mechanisms. A further three triplets occupy the moderate-evidence zone 0 .20 Ōēż PIP < 0.50: 

AKR1C3 ŌĆōPTGDR (0.377), CLEC2B ŌĆōKLRF1 (0.249), and IL23A ŌĆōIL12RB1 (0.204). The remaining 30 triplets fall below PIP = 0 .20, with the large majority at or below PIP = 0 .10. Both the discoveries and the most confidently absent signals are biologically interpretable, as discussed below.

Moderate-evidence signals. Three triplets in the 0 .20ŌĆō0 .50 PIP range warrant atten-tion as candidates for replication in larger cohorts. AKR1C3 ŌĆōPTGDR (PIP = 0.377) pairs the aldo-keto reductase AKR1C3 20 , a prostaglandin-biosynthetic enzyme, with the PGD 2

receptor PTGDR 18 on monocytes, placing it squarely within the prostaglandin signaling theme of this axis. CLEC2B ŌĆōKLRF1 (PIP = 0.249) nominally pairs an NK activating lig-and with its cognate receptor; however, as KLRF1 (NKp80) is predominantly expressed on NK cells rather than monocytes 21 , this sub-threshold signal most plausibly reflects an inci-dental instrument correlation rather than a genuine NK ŌåÆMonocyte communication event. 

IL23A ŌĆōIL12RB1 (PIP = 0.204) shows suggestive evidence for IL-23/IL-12 receptor cross-signaling, consistent with the structural homology between these cytokine families and their shared receptor subunit 22 .

Absent signals and biological specificity. A key strength of MR-CCC is its ability to assign near-zero posterior probability to biologically implausible signals, providing an intrinsic specificity calibration that complements the discovery set. All ten ICAM adhe-sion pairs annotated in CellPhoneDB ŌĆö involving ICAM1 , ICAM2 , ICAM3 , and ICAM4 

paired with ITGAL , ITGB2 , ITGAM , and ITGAX ŌĆö returned PIPs Ōēż 0.18, consistent with the expectation that ICAM-mediated adhesion requires direct cellŌĆōcell contact 23 and does not operate as a soluble signaling mechanism propagated through NK-cell ligand ex-pression. IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA (PIP = 0.07) and IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB (PIP = 0.06) are near zero: IL-15 is principally produced by monocytes and dendritic cells to sustain NK cell homeostasis 24 ,and its absence in the NK ŌåÆMonocyte direction correctly reflects this established biological directionality. IL6 ŌĆōIL6ST (PIP = 0.026) and WNT7A ŌĆōFZD3 (PIP = 0.027) likewise show negligible posterior support, appropriate for pathways not associated with NK cell effer-ent signaling 25 . Directional specificity is further illustrated by cross-axis comparison with the Monocytes ŌåÆ CD4 + T cell axis (Supplementary Section S2.5.2): SEMA4D ŌĆōCD72 26 ,14 which achieves PIP = 0.674 in the Monocytes ŌåÆCD4 + direction, returns PIP = 0.056 in the NK ŌåÆMonocytes direction. This pair-specific, direction-specific posterior contrast demon-strates that MR-CCC recovers causal signals tied to senderŌĆōreceiver identity rather than simply flagging co-expressed ligandŌĆōreceptor pairs irrespective of directionality.

┬Ę (Z/ sd( Z)) across the ob-served donor range for the eight discovery triplets, grouped by pathway class. The four panels show qualitatively distinct modulation profiles: the diverging IL-18 receptor chains (ampli-fication through IL18R1 , reversal through IL18RAP ), the EP4-versus-EP2 prostaglandin contrast, the GABA-B activation-to-inhibition crossover near the population mean, and the parallel decline of both IFNG receptor chains in the upper receptor tercile. 

Summary. The eight NK cells ŌåÆ monocytes discoveries span four pathway classes (GABA, interferon, interleukin, prostaglandin) with biologically coherent receptor modulation, while implausible signals (ICAM adhesion, reversed IL-15) correctly receive near-zero PIPs. Re-sults for the remaining 19 ordered cell-type pairs are in Supplementary Materials (Sec-tion S2). Two cross-direction patterns merit note: the IL-18 opposing-chain pattern is par-tially mirrored in the CD8 + T cells ŌåÆ monocytes direction (Supplementary Section S2.3.4), suggesting a receptor stoichiometry-dependent tuning mechanism general to cytotoxic lym-phocyte senders; and the NK ŌåÆ monocytes axis (8 discoveries) is the most evidence-rich directional axis in the 20-pair panel, far exceeding the reverse direction, consistent with NK cells as primary cytokine effectors in innate immune regulation. 

## 3 Discussion 

Inferring biologically meaningful CCC from transcriptomic data remains challenging because ligand expression, receptor expression, and downstream pathway activity may all be influ-enced by shared unmeasured confounding. Existing methods primarily rely on association patterns and do not distinguish causal signaling from correlated expression driven by con-founders. We introduced MR-CCC, a Bayesian Mendelian randomization framework that 15 integrates instrumental variables, receptor-modulated effect modeling, and probabilistic vari-able selection to enable causal inference of intercellular communication. MR-CCC shifts CCC analysis from an associational paradigm toward a causal, mechanistically grounded frame-work in which the fundamental question is not whether ligand and receptor expression are jointly elevated, but whether variation in ligand expression mechanically drives downstream pathway activity through receptor engagement. MR-CCC advances current approaches in three key respects. First, it leverages cis-eQTL instruments for both ligand and receptor expression, mitigating bias from unmeasured con-founding that would otherwise propagate into effect estimates and communication scores. Second, it explicitly models receptor-dependent modulation through an interaction term, allowing the strength and direction of ligand effects to vary with receptor expression in the receiving cell; this structure is identifiable under standard MR assumptions (Proposition 1). Third, the spikeŌĆōandŌĆōslab prior yields posterior inclusion probabilities that serve as an in-terpretable, calibrated communication score. The simulation results demonstrate that these three properties are jointly necessary for reliable inference under confounding. In the null scenario, MR-CCC suppresses spurious signals, maintaining near-zero PIPs, negligible rejection rates, and accurate parameter esti-mates across all sample sizes. OLS, which is an association-based method, fails entirely: it assigns the maximum communication score and rejects in every replicate regardless of sample size, confirming that the associational paradigm is fundamentally compromised under even moderate unmeasured confounding. MVMR corrects confounding bias in estimation but does not fully resolve the false-discovery problem, as null communication scores remain elevated due to residual correlation between the instrumented ligand exposure and the outcome. MR-BMA achieves low null scores via Bayesian model selection but incurs a persistent structural bias in the ligand effect estimate, attributable to the missing interaction term, and pro-vides no estimate of the receptor-modulated effect. MR-CCC is the only evaluated approach that simultaneously achieves strong null calibration, MR-based confounding correction, and joint regularized estimation of the full communication effect vector. When communication is present, MR-CCC retains high detection power with stable estimation of both the main 16 and interaction effects across all sample sizes and signal scenarios. Application to OneK1K illustrates the biological specificity of MR-CCC. Along the most evidence-rich axis (NK cells ŌåÆ monocytes), MR-CCCŌĆÖs explicit interaction model uncovered findings inaccessible to additive frameworks: opposing receptor-modulation signs across the two obligate IL-18 receptor subunits 9,10 , indicating a receptor stoichiometry-dependent tun-ing of IL-18 signaling, and co-discovery of both obligate IFN-╬│ receptor chains 16 , which must heterodimerize to signal ŌĆö internal validation that confounding-driven signals would not produce. The framework also assigned near-zero posterior probability to biologically implausible signals: ICAM adhesion pairs 23 (no soluble mechanism), the reversed IL-15 di-rection 24 (monocyte-to-NK biology), and SEMA4D ŌĆōCD72 26 , a high-confidence discovery in the Monocytes ŌåÆ CD4 + T direction returning PIP = 0.056 here, demonstrating senderŌĆō receiver-specific inference. More broadly, modeling pathway activity as the outcome links ligandŌĆōreceptor interac-tions to downstream functional programs in the receiving cell. Rather than reporting a single interaction score per pair, MR-CCC produces pathway-resolved communication signals that are statistically supported and directly interpretable in terms of the biological programs they engage, supporting the construction of causally annotated communication networks that can guide experimental prioritization. Several extensions may further enhance the framework. Future work could develop cell-state-resolved formulations that preserve within-donor variation, enabling detection of com-munication signals that differ across discrete cell states or continuous transcriptional tra-jectories rather than capturing only cell population-average effects. A second direction is to incorporate hierarchical structure across pathways or cell-type pairs, sharing information across related triplets while preserving context-specific effects. A third is to jointly model multiple ligands or receptors to study coordinated or higher-order signaling patterns. Fi-nally, integrating alternative outcome representations for nonlinear or non-Gaussian pathway behavior may improve robustness in complex settings, and the demonstrated specificity of MR-CCC suggests its use as a principled screening filter to complement, rather than replace, existing co-expression pipelines. 17 In summary, MR-CCC provides a principled, instrument-based framework for causal inference of receptor-modulated CCC. By integrating MR with interaction modeling and Bayesian variable selection, it establishes a causal, pathway-aware approach to intercellular signaling that moves beyond correlational analyses toward statistically rigorous and mecha-nistically interpretable causal CCC. 

## 4 Methods 

Consider an ordered pair of cell types, with one acting as the putative sender and the other as the receiver. The goal is to determine whether variation in ligand expression in the sender cell type causes the change of pathway activity in the receiver cell type, while allowing this effect to be moderated by receptor expression. For donor i = 1 , . . . , n , let Xi denote ligand expression in the sender cell, Zi receptor expression in the receiver cell, Yi pathway activity in the receiver cell, Gi cis-eQTL instruments for Xi, Hi cis-eQTL instruments for Zi, Vi ob-served donor-level covariates, and Ui any unmeasured confounders. Because germline genetic variants are fixed at conception, they are largely independent of environmental confounding, and provide a basis for causal identification via MR.

4.2.2 Posterior Inference 

Posterior inference proceeds via a Gibbs sampler with closed-form full conditionals for ev-ery parameter. At each iteration, the sampler updates the first-stage exposure parame-ters ( ŽĆX , ╬▒ X , Žā 2 

> X

) and ( ŽĆZ , ╬▒ Z , Žā 2 

> Z

); then recomputes the plug-in conditional means XŌłŚ =

> Y

); and finally updates ╬▓ | ╬│,the inclusion indicator ╬│, and the inclusion probability Žü. All matrix inverses are regularized by a small ridge term ╬╗ > 0 for numerical stability. The full conditional distributions and the complete sampling scheme are given in Supplementary Materials (Section S1); the sampler is implemented in Rcpp for computational efficiency. Posterior summaries are the posterior means of ╬▓X , ╬▓ XZ and the posterior inclusion probability PIP = Pr( ╬│ = 1 | data).

4.4 Simulation: Competing Methods 

We compared MR-CCC against three alternative approaches. 21 (1) OLS (naive regression). We fitted 

Yi = ╬╝ + ╬▓X Xi + ╬▓Z Zi + ╬▓XZ XiZi + V ŌŖż 

> i

╬▒Y + ╬Ąi

by ordinary least squares, ignoring the instrumental variables and therefore not correcting for unmeasured confounding. The communication score is 1 ŌłÆ pF , where pF is the p-value from a joint F -test of H0 : ╬▓X = ╬▓XZ = 0: 

F = 12 (C ╦å╬▓)ŌŖżC dVar( ╦å╬▓) CŌŖżŌłÆ1(C ╦å╬▓), pF = P  F (2 , n ŌłÆ p) > F obs 

,

where C is the 2 ├Ś p contrast matrix selecting ╬▓X and ╬▓XZ from the OLS coefficient vector. Communication is declared when pF Ōēż 0.05. 

(2) MVMR (multivariable Mendelian randomization). We applied MVMR 5. First, ligand and receptor expressions were each regressed on the full instrument set [ G, H ] and covariates V by OLS to obtain fitted values ╦åX and ╦åZ. Then, the outcome was regressed on ╦åX, ╦åZ, and covariates by OLS. The communication score is 1 ŌłÆ pt, where pt is the p-value of the t-test for H0 : ╬▓X = 0; communication is declared when pt Ōēż 0.05. MVMR corrects for unmeasured confounding through MR but relies on a fixed frequentist significance threshold, does not model the ligandŌĆōreceptor interaction, and does not impose a structured prior on the communication effect. 

(3) MR-BMA (Bayesian model averaging MR). We applied the Bayesian model averaging approach of 6. For each instrument gj Ōłł [G, H ], one-sample summary statistics ( ╦å╬▓Xj , ╦å╬▓Zj , ╦å╬▓Y j ) and their standard errors were obtained by simple OLS. With ligand X and receptor Z as the two candidate exposures, MR-BMA enumerates all 2 2 = 4 exposure in-clusion models, assigns a g-prior Bayes factor to each model, normalizes to posterior model probabilities, and extracts the marginal inclusion probability (MIP) and model-averaged causal effect (MACE) for each exposure. The communication score is MIP X , the poste-rior probability that the ligand has a nonzero causal effect on the pathway; communication is declared when MIP X > 0.5. Crucially, MR-BMA operates on per-instrument summary statistics and models only additive effects of the two exposures; it does not model the ligandŌĆō receptor interaction ╬▓XZ , and estimates of this parameter are unavailable from this method. 22 (4) MR-CCC. We applied the Gibbs sampler described in Section 4.2. The posterior inclusion probability PIP = Pr( ╬│ = 1 | data) served as the natural communication score; communication is declared when PIP > 0.5. Posterior means of ╬▓X and ╬▓XZ were used as point estimates. The sampler was run for 20,000 iterations with a 2,000-iteration burn-in and a thinning factor of 5. MR-CCC is the only method that simultaneously (i) corrects for unmeasured confounding via MR, (ii) performs Bayesian model selection over the presence of communication, and (iii) provides regularized joint estimates of both ╬▓X and ╬▓XZ .

4.5 Simulation: Performance Metrics 

Communication score and rejection rule. Each method produces a scalar communi-cation score on [0 , 1]. For MR-CCC the score is PIP = Pr( ╬│ = 1 | data), a Bayesian posterior probability. For MR-BMA the score is MIP X , likewise a Bayesian quantity. For OLS the score is 1 ŌłÆ pF , the complement of the joint F -test p-value for H0 : ╬▓X = ╬▓XZ = 0. For MVMR the score is 1 ŌłÆ pt, the complement of the t-test p-value for H0 : ╬▓X = 0. Neither is a probability, but both place all four methods on a common [0 , 1] scale for visualization. Bayesian methods declare communication when the respective score exceeds 0.5; frequentist methods declare communication when the corresponding p-value is Ōēż 0.05. For each scenario, sample size, and method we report: (i) mean communication score with standard deviation and (ii) rejection rate across the 20 replicates. 

Parameter estimation. For ╬▓X and ╬▓XZ , we recorded the point estimate from each method in every replicate. For MR-BMA, ╬▓X is the MACE; ╬▓XZ is not estimable (denoted ŌĆ£ŌĆöŌĆØ). For MVMR, ╬▓XZ is likewise not estimated as it is not included in the standard formulation. We computed bias (signed deviation from the true value) and mean absolute deviation (MAD) across the 20 replicates. Results are reported in Tables 1ŌĆō3. 23 4.6 Real-Data Analysis: Data Preparation and Instrument Selec-tion 

Dataset. The OneK1K cohort 7 comprises donor-matched germline genotype data and single-cell RNA sequencing profiles for 982 donors across five major peripheral immune cell types: B cells, CD4 + T cells, CD8 + T cells, natural killer (NK) cells, and monocytes. For each ordered sender ŌåÆreceiver pair we evaluated ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets in which ligand expression was measured in the sender cell type and receptor expression and pathway activity were obtained in the receiver cell type. 

Preprocessing and donor-level expression construction. Raw single-cell RNA counts were aggregated to donor-level gene expression matrices by summing counts across all cells of a given type per donor. Donor-specific library sizes were computed within each cell type, normalized to the cell-type median, and used to scale donor-level expression values. Donors were excluded if their library size exceeded the median plus three median absolute deviations, or fell below 25% of the median, in either the sender or receiver cell type. After filtering, the NK cells ŌåÆ Monocytes analysis retained 651 donors. For each triplet, ligand expression X

was the normalized donor-level expression of the ligand gene in NK cells; receptor expression 

Z the corresponding gene in monocytes; and pathway activity Y a donor-level scalar derived from the pathway gene set in monocytes. 

LigandŌĆōreceptor and pathway definitions. Candidate ligandŌĆōreceptor pairs were ob-tained from CellPhoneDB 1. Pathway annotations were taken from MSigDB Reactome gene sets 28 . After restricting to genes present in the filtered expression matrices and triplets with valid cis-eQTL instruments, the analysis yielded 41 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets spanning 11 biological pathways. 

Pathway activity construction and instrument selection. For each Reactome gene set in monocytes, donor-level pathway activity was summarized using six complementary representations: first principal component, mean expression, AUCell 29 , UCell 30 , ssGSEA 31 ,24 and GSVA 32 . The representation with the strongest absolute association with ligand ex-pression was retained for each triplet. Candidate cis-SNPs were identified within a ┬▒200 kb promoter-centred window for each ligand and receptor gene, screened by regressing donor-level expression on genotype dosage, adjusting for age, sex, and the first three genotype principal components (these variables are also used as covariates in MR-CCC), and ranked by association strength. Up to ten top cis-SNPs per gene were used as instruments; triplets lacking valid instruments for either gene were excluded. 

## Data availability 

Preprocessed donor-level single-cell RNA-seq expression matrices and genotype data from the OneK1K cohort used in this study are publicly available on Zenodo at https://doi.org/ 10.5281/zenodo.19675075 . The original OneK1K genotype and scRNA-seq data are avail-able from the study authors ( https://onek1k.org ) under the original data access terms 7.LigandŌĆōreceptor annotations were obtained from CellPhoneDB v5 1; pathway gene sets from MSigDB 28 .

## Code availability 

All analysis code, including the Gibbs sampler ( mr ccc gibbs.cpp ), simulation scripts ( simulation mrccc.R ), database construction ( build lr database.R )and real-data analysis ( real data analysis.R ) is publicly available at https://github. com/bitansa/MR-CCC under the MIT License.

## S2 Real Data Results for Additional Ordered Cell-Type Pairs 

The main manuscript presents the results for the NK cells ŌåÆ Monocytes axis. Here we report the results for the remaining 19 ordered sender ŌåÆ receiver pairs among the five pe-ripheral immune cell types profiled in the OneK1K cohort 1. Data preprocessing, donor-level 3expression construction, cis-eQTL instrument selection, and model fitting follow exactly the same pipeline described in main paper. For each ordered pair we display three figures: (i) the PIP ranking across all evaluated ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets; (ii) the bubble plot of standardized posterior main and interaction effects; and (iii) the receptor-modulated effect curves for the high-PIP triplets. 

S2.1 B Cells as Sender 

S2.1.1 B Cells ŌåÆ CD4 + T Cells 

Across 868 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the B cell (sender) to CD4 + T cell (receiver) direction and identified three high-confidence causal com-munication signals with posterior inclusion probability (PIP) exceeding the discovery thresh-old of 0.5: IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA within the Interleukin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .867), LIPA ŌĆō

RORA within the Cholesterol signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .686), and SLC6A6 ŌĆōGABBR1 

within the GABA signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .54) (Figures S1ŌĆōS3). The strongest signal, IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA (PIP = 0 .867), reflects the well-characterized mech-anism of IL-15 transpresentation, in which antigen-presenting cells, including B cells, display IL-15 on their surface via IL-15R ╬▒ for recognition by neighboring CD4 + T cells 2,3 . IL-15 is a pleiotropic cytokine that promotes T cell survival, proliferation, and memory formation, with its bioavailability tightly controlled by IL-15R ╬▒-mediated transpresentation 4. The estimated main effect is negative ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ1.13), while the receptor-modulated interaction is large and positive ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 2 .28), producing an effect curve that crosses zero near the population-mean 

IL15RA expression level. CD4 + T cells expressing IL15RA above this mean therefore ex-hibit a progressively positive causal response to B cell IL-15 production, consistent with IL-15R ╬▒-dependent co-stimulation that amplifies with receptor abundance. The second discovered triplet, LIPA ŌĆōRORA (PIP = 0 .686), connects B cell lysosomal acid lipase A ( LIPA ) activityŌĆöwhich releases free cholesterol and fatty acids from intracellular lipid esters 5ŌĆöto RORA signaling in CD4 + T cells. RORA is a nuclear receptor activated by cholesterol metabolites and oxysterols that negatively regulates inflammatory NF-╬║B4signaling and shapes helper T cell differentiation 6,7 . Both the main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.682) and the interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ2.40) are negative, yielding a monotonically decreasing effect curve: B cell lipid-catabolic activity exerts a progressively stronger suppressive influence on CD4 +

T cell downstream pathway activity as RORA expression rises. This pattern suggests that B cell-derived cholesterol metabolites engage RORA -mediated anti-inflammatory programs in CD4 + T cells in a receptor dose-dependent manner. The third discovered triplet, SLC6A6 ŌĆōGABBR1 (PIP = 0 .54), exhibits a near-zero main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .014) alongside a large positive interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 2 .01), yielding an almost purely receptor-dependent effect curve that passes through zero at the mean and rises steeply. 

SLC6A6 encodes the taurine and ╬▓-alanine transporter; taurine is a known partial agonist of GABA receptors and provides a mechanistic link between B cell amino-acid transport and GABA-B receptor activation on CD4 + T cells 8. GABA-B receptor signaling has been shown to suppress T cell activation and proliferation in a receptor density-dependent manner 9,consistent with the purely interaction-driven pattern observed here: the communication signal is essentially absent when GABBR1 expression is at or below the population mean and emerges only in CD4 + T cells with elevated receptor levels. Notably, several biologically implausible triplets received near-zero PIPs, providing im-plicit validation of the modelŌĆÖs specificity. Interferon-╬│ (IFNG ) paired with either of its receptors ( IFNGR1 , PIP = 0 .043; IFNGR2 , PIP = 0 .033) ranked near the bottom of the PIP distribution, consistent with the well-established fact that IFN-╬│ is produced primarily by Th1 CD4 + and CD8 + T cells rather than B cells, making B cells an implausible sender in this axis 10 . The CCL28 ŌĆōCCR10 pair (PIP = 0 .029) similarly received one of the lowest PIPs: CCL28 ŌĆōCCR10 mediates homing of T cells to skin and mucosal epithelia rather than peripheral lymphoid communication, and this tissue-specific axis is not expected to be ac-tive in peripheral blood donors 11,12 . Finally, the WNT7A ŌĆōFZD3 pair (PIP = 0 .028) received the lowest PIP of all 42 triplets; WNT signaling between B cells and CD4 + T cells has no established biological basis in peripheral blood 13 .50.69 0.54 0.87

ŌåÆ CD4 + T cells analysis. Only the three discovery pairs (PIP > 0.5) are displayed, grouped into the three pathway panels with confirmed discoveries (Signaling by Cholesterol, Signaling by GABA, and Signaling by Interleukin). In the Signaling by Interleukin panel, the IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA curve is steeply increasing and crosses zero near the mean receptor level, reflecting a receptor-dependent sign switch from suppression to activation. In the Signal-ing by Cholesterol panel, the LIPA ŌĆōRORA curve is monotonically decreasing, indicating receptor-amplified suppression that strengthens as RORA expression rises. Across 845 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the B cell (sender) to CD8 + T cell (receiver) direction and identified two high-confidence causal com-munication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5: IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA (PIP = 0 .554) and IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB 

(PIP = 0 .518), both within the Interleukin signaling pathway (Figures S4ŌĆōS6). Both dis-coveries implicate B cell-derived IL-15 as a causal communicator to CD8 + T cells, engaging two distinct receptor chains of the IL-15/IL-2 receptor complex. The IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA triplet (PIP = 0 .554) recapitulates the IL-15 transpresentation axis identified in the B cells ŌåÆ CD4 + T cells direction, here operating on CD8 + T cells. IL-15 displayed on B cell surfaces via IL-15R ╬▒ delivers homeostatic survival and proliferation signals to CD8 + T cells, a mechanism well established to be indispensable for the maintenance of virus-specific memory CD8 + T cells 4,14 . Both the estimated main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .662) and the receptor-modulated interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 0 .589) are positive, yielding a monotonically increasing effect curve: CD8 + T cells expressing higher levels of IL15RA show a uniformly stronger positive causal response to B cell IL-15 production, with no sign reversal across the observed receptor expression range. The second discovered triplet, IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB (PIP = 0 .518), engages the IL-2R ╬▓ chain (en-coded by IL2RB ; also known as CD122), which is shared between the IL-15 and IL-2 receptor complexes 4. On CD8 + T cells, signaling through the IL-2R ╬▓/╬│c heterodimer supports home-ostatic and antigen-driven proliferation 15 . The positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .796) indicates that B cell IL-15 production generally up-regulates downstream Interleukin pathway activity in CD8 + T cells; the negative receptor-modulated interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ0.647) reveals that this stimulatory effect is progressively attenuated in cells with high IL2RB expression. The effect curve crosses zero near Ōł╝1.2 standard deviations above the population-mean IL2RB 

level and becomes mildly suppressive at the highest receptor densities, consistent with sig-naling saturation or competitive displacement by IL-2 at the shared IL-2R ╬▓ chain in CD8 +

T cells that strongly up-regulate this subunit. Notably, several triplets received near-zero PIPs. IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .032) and 

IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 (PIP = 0 .032) remained at the bottom of the distribution, consistent with 9B cells not being a physiological source of IFN-╬│ in peripheral blood 10 . The LIPA ŌĆōRORA 

triplet, which reached PIP = 0 .686 in the B cells ŌåÆ CD4 + T cells direction, fell to PIP = 0 .191 here, suggesting that B cell-derived cholesterol-catabolic signals preferentially engage 

RORA -mediated immunomodulatory programs in helper T cells rather than cytotoxic T cells, consistent with RORA ŌĆÖs established role in Th17/Treg balance 7. Similarly, SLC6A6 ŌĆō

GABBR1 , which was discovered in the B cells ŌåÆ CD4 + T cells direction (PIP = 0 .54), received a PIP of only 0.035 here, indicating that the GABA-B receptor-mediated inhibitory axis from B cell taurine transport operates in a CD4 +-selective manner. 10 0.55 0.52

Across 818 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the B cell (sender) to NK cell (receiver) direction and identified three high-confidence causal com-munication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5: IL6 ŌĆōIL6ST within the Interleukin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .972), PTGES3 ŌĆōPTGER2 within the Prostaglandin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .556), and ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE2 within the Integrin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .506) (Figures S7ŌĆōS9). All three discoveries are characterized by large receptor-modulated inter-action terms whose sign reversal occurs near the population-mean receptor expression level, indicating that the direction as well as the magnitude of each B cell communication effect is gated by recipient NK cell receptor density. The dominant signal, IL6 ŌĆōIL6ST (PIP = 0 .972), identifies B cell-derived IL-6 as a causal regulator of NK cell Interleukin pathway activity mediated through the signal-transducing subunit gp130 (encoded by IL6ST ). B cells are well-established producers of IL-6, partic-ularly following TLR or BCR activation, and IL-6 engages gp130-containing receptor com-plexes to activate the JAK1/JAK2ŌĆōSTAT1/STAT3 cascade in target cells 16 . The modest positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .394) combined with a large negative interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ2.09) yields an effect curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .19 standard deviations above the mean IL6ST level and then becomes steeply negative. NK cells expressing IL6ST at or above the population mean therefore experience a progressively stronger suppressive effect of B cell IL-6 on NK cell Interleukin pathway gene expression, consistent with IL-6ŌĆÖs docu-mented ability to inhibit NK cell cytotoxicity and effector programs when gp130-mediated signaling is sustained 17 .The second discovered triplet, PTGES3 ŌĆōPTGER2 (PIP = 0 .556), links B cell prostaglandin E synthase 3 ( PTGES3 )ŌĆöa cytosolic enzyme that converts prostaglandin H 2 to prostaglandin E2 (PGE 2)ŌĆöto the EP2 prostaglandin receptor (encoded by PTGER2 ) on NK cells. PGE 2

signaling through the EP2 receptor activates the adenylyl cyclaseŌĆōcAMPŌĆōPKA axis, a well-characterized suppressor of NK cell cytotoxicity and IFN-╬│ production 18 . The negative main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.416) and positive interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 1 .57) produce a curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .26 standard deviations above the mean PTGER2 level. NK 14 cells with low EP2 expression show a net suppressive response to B cell PGE 2 output, while NK cells expressing PTGER2 above this threshold show progressive up-regulation of their own Prostaglandin pathway activity, consistent with a PGE 2ŌĆōEP2 feed-forward mechanism in which receptor-replete NK cells amplify prostaglandin signaling in response to B cell-derived PGE 2.The third discovered triplet, ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE2 (PIP = 0 .506), implicates a direct ad-hesion contact between B cell integrin ╬▒V ( ITGAV ) and the adhesion G protein-coupled receptor EMR2 (encoded by ADGRE2 ) on NK cells. ADGRE2 (EMR2) carries extracellu-lar EGF-like domains that serve as integrin counter-ligands mediating cellŌĆōcell contact, and is expressed on NK cells and myeloid cells in peripheral blood 19 . The small positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .136) and large negative interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ1.47) yield a curve that crosses zero within 0 .1 standard deviations of the mean ADGRE2 expression level and becomes strongly negative at high receptor density. NK cells expressing high levels of ADGRE2 therefore experience a strongly suppressive effect of B cell ╬▒V integrin engagement, suggesting that 

╬▒VŌĆōEMR2 contact at the BŌĆōNK cell interface inhibits NK cell Integrin pathway activity in an ADGRE2 dose-dependent manner. Notably, several triplets received low PIPs. IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA (PIP = 0 .373) and IL15 ŌĆō

IL2RB (PIP = 0 .353) were the highest-ranking non-discovered signals but fell below the discovery threshold, suggesting that B cells are not a dominant cellular source of transp-resented IL-15 for NK cells in peripheral blood; the primary providers of NK cell-directed IL-15 are dendritic cells and macrophages 3,14 . IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .171) and IFNG ŌĆō

IFNGR2 (PIP = 0 .060) again received near-zero support, consistent with B cells not being a physiological source of IFN-╬│ in peripheral blood 10 .15 0.97 0.56 0.51 

PIP = 0.5

In the Signaling by Integrin panel, the ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE2 curve crosses zero near the mean and becomes strongly negative at high ADGRE2 expression. 18 S2.1.4 B Cells ŌåÆ Monocytes 

Across 665 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 41 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the B cell (sender) to Monocyte (receiver) direction and identified two high-confidence causal commu-nication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5: ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAX within the Adhesion by ICAM pathway (PIP = 0 .562) and IL6 ŌĆōIL6ST within the Interleukin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .554) (Figures S10ŌĆōS12). Both discoveries exhibit a strong receptor-modulated interac-tion relative to the main ligand effect, and both yield sign-reversing effect curves near the population-mean receptor expression level. The top-ranked triplet, ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAX (PIP = 0 .562), implicates B cell intercellu-lar adhesion molecule 1 (ICAM-1, encoded by ICAM1 ) as a causal regulator of monocyte Adhesion pathway activity through integrin ╬▒X (CD11c, encoded by ITGAX ). ICAM-1 is constitutively expressed on B cells and is further up-regulated upon activation; it serves as the canonical counter- receptor for ╬▓2 integrins on myeloid cells 20 . CD11c ( ╬▒X chain) pairs with ╬▓2 (CD18) to form p150,95 (CR4), a complement receptor expressed at high levels on classical monocytes and conventional dendritic cells 21 . The positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .291) and large negative interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ2.04) yield a curve that crosses zero approximately 0.14 standard deviations above the mean ITGAX expression level and becomes strongly negative at high receptor density. Monocytes expressing ITGAX below this threshold show a modestly positive Adhesion pathway response to B cell ICAM-1, whereas monocytes with high CD11c expressionŌĆöa phenotype associated with a more differentiated, dendritic cell-like stateŌĆöexperience a progressively stronger suppressive effect of B cell ICAM-1 engagement on their Adhesion pathway activity, consistent with contact-mediated restraint of DC-like monocyte activation through sustained ╬▒X╬▓2ŌĆōICAM-1 ligation. The second discovered triplet, IL6 ŌĆōIL6ST (PIP = 0 .554), again identifies B cell-derived IL-6 signaling through gp130 ( IL6ST ) as a causal communication axis, paralleling the dis-covery in the B cells ŌåÆ NK cells direction. However, the receptor-modulated interaction term here is large and positive ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 1 .35), in contrast to the large negative interac-tion observed for NK cells ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ2.09). The modest positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .153) combined with the positive interaction produces a curve that crosses zero approximately 19 0.11 standard deviations below the mean IL6ST level, making the effect positive across essentially the full observed receptor expression range and increasingly so at high gp130 density. Monocytes expressing high levels of IL6ST therefore show a strongly amplified stimulatory response to B cell IL-6, consistent with the well-established role of IL-6/gp130 signaling in promoting monocyte and macrophage pro-inflammatory activation, acute-phase responses, and cytokine production 16,22 . The direction-specific sign of the IL6ST interac-tion termŌĆöactivating for monocytes, suppressive for NK cellsŌĆöreflects the fundamentally different downstream consequences of sustained gp130 signaling in myeloid versus innate lymphoid cell types. Notably, several triplets received near-zero PIPs. IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .047) and 

IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 (PIP = 0 .032) remained at the bottom of the distribution, again consistent with B cells not being a physiological source of IFN-╬│ in peripheral blood 10 . IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA 

(PIP = 0 .143) and IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB (PIP = 0 .167) both fell well below the discovery thresh-old, consistent with monocytes not being primary targets of IL-15-mediated homeostatic signaling; IL-15 acts principally on T and NK cells rather than on circulating monocytes 4.20 0.56 0.55

S2.2.1 CD4 + T Cells ŌåÆ B Cells 

Across 868 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the CD4 + Tcell (sender) to B cell (receiver) direction and identified ten high-confidence causal commu-nication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5 (Figures S13ŌĆōS15), the largest number of discoveries in any senderŌĆōreceiver direction analyzed here. The ten triplets span four pathway classes: six Adhesion by ICAM pairs ( ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAL , PIP = 0 .658; ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAM , PIP = 0 .639; 

ICAM2 ŌĆōITGAL , PIP = 0 .947; ICAM2 ŌĆōITGB2 , PIP = 0 .749; ICAM3 ŌĆōITGAL , PIP = 0 .504; 

ICAM4 ŌĆōITGAL , PIP = 0 .593), two Signaling by Integrin pairs ( ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE5 , PIP = 0 .992; ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 , PIP = 0 .606), one Signaling by Interleukin triplet ( IL23A ŌĆō

IL12RB1 , PIP = 0 .798), and one Signaling by Thromboxane triplet ( TBXAS1 ŌĆōTBXA2R ,PIP = 0 .595). 

Adhesion by ICAM signals. The six discovered ICAMŌĆōintegrin triplets collectively re-flect the central role of adhesion molecule contacts at the CD4 + T cellŌĆōB cell immunological synapse, where ICAM family members on T cells engage ╬▓2 integrins on B cells to stabilize antigen-recognition and co-stimulatory interactions 20,23 . Despite sharing the same physi-cal interface, the six pairs exhibit strikingly heterogeneous receptor-modulated interaction terms, producing a characteristic fan of effect curves in the Adhesion by ICAM panel (Fig-ure S15). ICAM2 ŌĆōITGAL (PIP = 0 .947) and ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAM (PIP = 0 .639) both show sign-reversing curves: negative main effects ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.368 and ŌłÆ0.614, respectively) com-bined with large positive interactions ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 2 .59 and 2 .25) mean that B cells expressing LFA-1 ( ITGAL ) or Mac-1 ( ITGAM ) above approximately 0.14 and 0.27 standard devia-tions above the population mean transition from a suppressed to a progressively stimulated Adhesion pathway response to T cell ICAM engagement. ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAL (PIP = 0 .658, ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.740, ╦å╬▓XZ = 0 .321) shows a predominantly suppressive curve with a modest pos-itive interaction that partially attenuates this suppression at the highest LFA-1 densities. 

ICAM2 ŌĆōITGB2 (PIP = 0 .749, ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.346, ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ0.241) is monotonically suppres-sive, with both a negative main effect and a negative interaction delivering a consistent 24 down-regulation of B cell Adhesion pathway activity regardless of ╬▓2 expression level. In contrast, ICAM3 ŌĆōITGAL (PIP = 0 .504, ╦å╬▓X = 0 .059, ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ4.79) and ICAM4 ŌĆōITGAL 

(PIP = 0 .593, ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.017, ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ5.65) carry the steepest negative interaction terms in the entire analysis, with near-zero main effects and dominant negative interactions that produce strongly receptor-amplified suppression: B cells with high LFA-1 expression expe-rience a steeply increasing suppression of Adhesion pathway activity upon contact with T cell ICAM3 or ICAM4. The co-discovery of stimulatory and suppressive ICAMŌĆōLFA-1 sig-nals through different ICAM ligands is consistent with the architectural organization of the immunological synapse, where different ICAM family members occupy distinct supramolec-ular activation cluster domains and fulfill complementary activation and negative-feedback roles 23 .

IntegrinŌĆōADGRE signals. The highest-PIP discovery in this direction, ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE5 

(PIP = 0 .992), implicates CD4 + T cell ╬▓1 integrin ( ITGB1 ) as a causal activator of B cell Integrin pathway activity through the adhesion G protein-coupled receptor CD97 (encoded by ADGRE5 ). CD97 is expressed on resting and activated B cells and serves as a mul-tifunctional adhesion receptor whose extracellular EGF-like domains mediate cellŌĆōcell con-tact 24 . Both the main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .498) and the interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 3 .63) are positive, yielding a monotonically increasing curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .14 standard deviations below the mean ADGRE5 level: across essentially the full observed receptor ex-pression range, T cell ╬▓1 integrin engagement potentiates B cell Integrin pathway activity, with this potentiation growing steeply in B cells expressing high CD97. The companion triplet ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 (PIP = 0 .606, ╦å╬▓X = 0 .309, ╦å╬▓XZ = 1 .48) shows a parallel, though weaker, stimulatory and interaction-amplified pattern through the related adhesion receptor EMR2 (encoded by ADGRE2 ), which also carries EGF-like counter-receptor domains 19 .

Interleukin signal. The IL23A ŌĆōIL12RB1 triplet (PIP = 0 .798) identifies CD4 + T cell-derived IL-23 subunit ╬▒ (IL23A , the p19 subunit) as a causal regulator of B cell Interleukin pathway activity through the IL-12R ╬▓1 chain (encoded by IL12RB1 ). IL-23 is assembled from IL-23A and the shared p40 subunit (IL-12B), and its cognate receptor complex on B cells incorporates IL-12R ╬▓1 as the signal-transducing shared chain 25 . The modest positive 25 main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .186) and large positive interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 3 .16) produce a curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .06 standard deviations below the mean IL12RB1 level, making the stimulatory effect positive across virtually the entire observed receptor expression range and strongly amplified in B cells with high IL-12R ╬▓1 expression. 

Thromboxane signal. TBXAS1 ŌĆōTBXA2R (PIP = 0 .595) links thromboxane A 2 synthase 1 ( TBXAS1 ) expressed in CD4 + T cells to the thromboxane A 2 receptor (TP receptor, en-coded by TBXA2R ) on B cells. Activated CD4 + T cells produce thromboxane A 2 (TXA 2)via TBXAS1, and TXA 2 signaling through TBXA2R on lymphocytes regulates cell activa-tion, migration, and cytokine production 26 . Both the main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.620) and the receptor-modulated interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ5.47) are negative, yielding a monotonically and steeply decreasing curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .11 standard deviations below the mean TBXA2R level. B cells expressing TBXA2R at or above the population mean therefore experience an increasingly strong suppression of their own Thromboxane pathway activity as CD4 + T cell TXA 2 production rises, consistent with a T cell-mediated negative-feedback loop that dampens B cell autologous thromboxane signaling in proportion to TP receptor density. 

Low-PIP pairs. IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .144) and IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 (PIP = 0 .123) both fell below the discovery threshold. Unlike the B cell sender directionŌĆöwhere the low PIPs reflect the fact that B cells are not a physiological IFN-╬│ sourceŌĆöthe low PIPs here reflect the cellular heterogeneity of the CD4 + T cell pool: only the Th1 subset produces IFN-╬│,and the population-averaged causal effect across mixed CD4 + T cell states is insufficient to clear the discovery threshold 10 . IL6 ŌĆōIL6ST (PIP = 0 .079) and IL6 ŌĆōIL6R (PIP = 0 .091) received near-zero support, indicating that CD4 + T cell IL-6 production does not constitute a strong causal signal to B cells via gp130 in this dataset. 26 0.66 0.64 0.95 0.75 0.50 0.59 0.80 0.59 0.61 0.99 

PIP = 0.5

ReceptorŌłÆmodulated ligand effects: CD4 + T cells ŌłÆ> B cells (MRŌłÆCCC) Figure S15: Receptor-modulated effect curves ( ╦å╬▓X + ╦å╬▓XZ ┬Ę Z/ SD( Z)) for the CD4 + Tcells ŌåÆ B cells analysis. and ICAM4 ŌĆōITGAL show the steepest negative slopes in the analysis. In the Signaling by Integrin panel, ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE5 and ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 both show steep positive-slope curves. In the Signaling by Interleukin panel, IL23A ŌĆōIL12RB1 rises steeply from near zero at the mean. In the Signaling by Thromboxane panel, TBXAS1 ŌĆōTBXA2R is the steepest declining curve, becoming strongly negative at high TBXA2R expression. 29 S2.2.2 CD4 + T Cells ŌåÆ CD8 + T Cells 

Across 882 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the CD4 + Tcell (sender) to CD8 + T cell (receiver) direction and identified three high-confidence causal communication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5: IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB within the Interleukin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .668), ICAM2 ŌĆōITGAL within the Adhesion by ICAM pathway (PIP = 0 .547), and SEMA4D ŌĆōPTPRC within the Semaphorin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .538) (Figures S16ŌĆōS18). The top-ranked discovery, IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB (PIP = 0 .668), implicates CD4 + T cell-derived IL-15 as a causal activator of CD8 + T cell Interleukin pathway activity through the IL-2R ╬▓

chain (encoded by IL2RB ; also known as CD122), which is shared between the IL-15 and IL-2 receptor complexes and supports homeostatic proliferation and memory maintenance in CD8 + T cells 4,14,15 . Both the main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .770) and the receptor-modulated interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 0 .614) are positive, yielding a monotonically increasing effect curve: the estimated causal effect is positive across the full observed range of IL2RB expression, with the zero crossing located at ZŌłŚ Ōēł ŌłÆ 1.25 standard deviations below the meanŌĆöwell outside the bulk of the observed distribution. CD8 + T cells expressing higher levels of the IL-2R ╬▓

chain therefore show a uniformly stronger and progressively amplified positive response to CD4 + T cell IL-15 production. The second discovered triplet, ICAM2 ŌĆōITGAL (PIP = 0 .547), links CD4 + T cell inter-cellular adhesion molecule 2 ( ICAM2 ) to LFA-1 ( ITGAL ) on CD8 + T cells. ICAMŌĆōLFA-1 contacts are a central stabilizing force at the T cellŌĆōT cell immunological interface, coordi-nating antigen-dependent and helper-driven cytotoxic T cell activation 20,23 . The negative main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.403) combined with a large positive interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 2 .17) produces a sign-reversing effect curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .19 standard deviations above the mean ITGAL level. CD8 + T cells expressing ITGAL below this threshold experience a net suppressive effect of CD4 + T cell ICAM2 engagement on their Adhesion pathway activity; above it, the direction flips to increasingly stimulatory, consistent with a context-dependent adhesion signal in which LFA-1 density gates the transition between inhibitory and activating CD4ŌĆōCD8 contact. 30 The third discovery, SEMA4D ŌĆōPTPRC (PIP = 0 .538), implicates CD100 (semaphorin 4D, encoded by SEMA4D ), a class IV transmembrane semaphorin expressed on activated CD4 + T cells, as a causal regulator of CD8 + T cell Semaphorin pathway activity through the receptor tyrosine phosphatase CD45 (encoded by PTPRC ). SEMA4D is known to modulate immune cell activation through engagement of plexin and co-receptor signaling complexes on lymphocytes, with established roles in T cell cross-talk and leukocyte recruitment 27 .The near-zero main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.041) and strongly positive interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 0 .907) produce a curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .05 standard deviations above the mean 

PTPRC levelŌĆöessentially at the population mean. The causal signal is therefore almost entirely interaction-driven: only in CD8 + T cells expressing PTPRC above the population mean does CD4 + T cell SEMA4D exert a meaningful positive effect, suggesting that CD45 expression level gates the permissiveness of CD8 + T cells to semaphorin-mediated signals from helper T cells. Notably, several triplets did not reach the discovery threshold. IL15 ŌĆōIL15RA (PIP = 0.473) was the highest-ranking non-discovered signal and a close near-miss; while the shared IL-2R ╬▓ chain was discovered (PIP = 0 .668), the transpresentation axis through IL-15R ╬▒

appears less dominant in this CD4 + sender direction, consistent with IL-15R ╬▒-mediated transpresentation being a function more characteristic of antigen-presenting cells such as B cells and dendritic cells 3,14 . LIPA ŌĆōRORA (PIP = 0 .419) was also a notable near-miss; this triplet was discovered in the B cells ŌåÆ CD4 + T cells direction (PIP = 0 .686) but does not clear the threshold here, consistent with CD4 + T cells expressing lower levels of lysosomal lipid-catabolic activity than B cells and thus transmitting a weaker cholesterol-metabolite signal 7. IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 (PIP = 0 .348) and IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .299) received moderate but sub-threshold support; unlike the B cell sender directionŌĆöwhere IFN-╬│ production is biologically implausibleŌĆöCD4 + Th1 cells are a bona fide source of IFN-

╬│, and the moderate PIPs here likely reflect attenuation of the population-level signal by the cellular heterogeneity of the CD4 + T cell pool across donors 10 .31 0.55 0.67 0.54

ReceptorŌłÆmodulated ligand effects: CD4 + T cells ŌłÆ> CD8 + T cells (MRŌłÆCCC) Figure S18: Receptor-modulated effect curves ( ╦å╬▓X + ╦å╬▓XZ ┬Ę Z/ SD( Z)) for the CD4 + Tcells ŌåÆ CD8 + T cells analysis. Only the three discovery pairs (PIP > 0.5) are displayed, grouped into the three pathway panels with confirmed discoveries (Adhesion by ICAM, Signaling by Interleukin, and Signaling by Semaphorin). In the Signaling by Interleukin panel, the IL15 ŌĆōIL2RB curve is monotonically increasing, remaining positive throughout the observed receptor range with a zero crossing near ŌłÆ1.25 standard deviations below the mean. In the Adhesion by ICAM panel, the ICAM2 ŌĆōITGAL curve crosses zero near +0 .19 standard deviations above the mean, transitioning from suppressive to increasingly activating at high LFA-1 densities. In the Signaling by Semaphorin panel, the SEMA4D ŌĆōPTPRC curve passes near zero at the mean and rises steeply, consistent with an almost purely interaction-driven signal gated by CD45 expression level. 34 S2.2.3 CD4 + T Cells ŌåÆ NK Cells 

Across 850 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the CD4 + Tcell (sender) to NK cell (receiver) direction and identified four high-confidence causal com-munication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5: ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 within the Integrin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .910), ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE5 within the Integrin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .858), PTGES3 ŌĆōPTGER2 within the Prostaglandin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .625), and IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 within the Interferon signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .542) (Figures S19ŌĆō S21). The top-ranked discovery, ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 (PIP = 0 .910), implicates CD4 + T cell ╬▓1

integrin ( ITGB1 ) as a causal regulator of NK cell Integrin pathway activity through the adhesion G protein-coupled receptor EMR2 (encoded by ADGRE2 ), which is expressed on NK cells and myeloid cells and carries extracellular EGF-like counter-receptor domains 19 .The positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .404) and large negative interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ2.67) produce a sign-reversing effect curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .15 standard deviations above the mean ADGRE2 expression level. NK cells with low EMR2 expression therefore experi-ence a net stimulatory response to CD4 + T cell ╬▓1 integrin engagement, while those above this threshold transition to a progressively suppressive effect that grows steeply with EMR2 density. Notably, the ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 triplet was also discovered in the CD4 + T cells ŌåÆ Bcells direction (PIP = 0 .606), but there the interaction term was positive ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 1 .48); the sign reversal of the interaction between receiver cell types illustrates the cell-type specificity of receptor-modulated causal communication detected by MR-CCC. The second discovered triplet, ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE5 (PIP = 0 .858), implicates CD4 + T cell 

╬▒V integrin ( ITGAV ) as a causal activator of NK cell Integrin pathway activity through the adhesion G protein-coupled receptor CD97 (encoded by ADGRE5 ), whose EGF-like ectodomain serves as a counter-receptor for multiple integrin species 24 . Both the main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .342) and the interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 3 .44) are positive, yielding a curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .10 standard deviations below the mean ADGRE5 level and is therefore positive across essentially the full observed receptor expression range, growing steeply with CD97 density. Together, ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 and ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE5 form a characteristic 35 crossing pair in the Signaling by Integrin panel of the effect-curve figure (Figure S21): the former descends steeply from positive to negative as receptor expression rises, while the latter rises steeply from near zero to strongly positive, producing an X-shaped intersection that reflects divergent receptor-modulated outcomes of two distinct integrinŌĆōadhesion-GPCR contacts on NK cell Integrin pathway activity. The third discovered triplet, PTGES3 ŌĆōPTGER2 (PIP = 0 .625), links CD4 + T cell prostaglandin E synthase 3 ( PTGES3 ) to the EP2 prostaglandin receptor (encoded by PT-GER2 ) on NK cells, recapitulating the same PGE 2ŌĆōEP2 axis identified in the B cells ŌåÆ NK cells direction (PIP = 0 .556). PGE 2 signaling through EP2 activates the adenylyl cyclaseŌĆō cAMPŌĆōPKA cascade, a well-characterized suppressor of NK cell cytotoxicity and effector cytokine production 18 . The negative main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = ŌłÆ0.532) and large positive interac-tion ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 2 .24) produce a curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .24 standard deviations above the mean PTGER2 level. NK cells with EP2 expression below this threshold expe-rience net suppression of their Prostaglandin pathway activity in response to CD4 + T cell PGE 2, while those with high EP2 expression show progressively stronger activation, consis-tent with a PGE 2ŌĆōEP2 feed-forward mechanism in which receptor-replete NK cells amplify prostaglandin signaling independently of the lymphocyte source. The fourth discovery, IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 (PIP = 0 .542), identifies CD4 + T cell-derived IFN-╬│ as a causal communicator to NK cells through the signal-transducing ╬▓ chain of the IFN-╬│ receptor complex (encoded by IFNGR2 )10,28 . This is the first direction in the present analysis in which an IFN-╬│ triplet clears the discovery threshold, consistent with CD4 + Th1 cells being a bona fide source of IFN-╬│ in peripheral bloodŌĆöunlike B cells, for which all IFN-

╬│ pairs received near-zero PIPs. The positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .274) reflects a baseline stimulatory IFN-╬│ signal on NK cell Interferon pathway activity; the negative interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ1.05) indicates that this stimulatory effect diminishes with increasing IFNGR2 

expression and crosses zero approximately 0 .26 standard deviations above the mean, becom-ing suppressive at the highest receptor densities, consistent with receptor-mediated negative feedback on sustained IFN-╬│ signaling 10 . The receptor-chain specificity of the discoveryŌĆö 

IFNGR2 discovered at PIP = 0 .542 while the ligand-binding ╬▒ chain IFNGR1 remained 36 sub-threshold at PIP = 0 .224ŌĆöpoints to the expression level of the signal-transducing ╬▓

chain as the primary determinant of the receptor-modulated interaction. Notably, several triplets did not reach the discovery threshold. IL1B ŌĆōIL1RAP (PIP = 0 .448) was the highest-ranking non-discovered triplet; IL-1 ╬▓ produced by activated CD4 +

T cells is a known activator of NK cell cytotoxicity and IFN-╬│ production through the IL-1 receptor accessory protein, but the population-level signal did not achieve consistent dis-covery strength 29 . ICAM1 ŌĆōITGAX (PIP = 0 .385) and SEMA4A ŌĆōPLXND1 (PIP = 0 .376) were notable near-misses within the Adhesion by ICAM and Semaphorin signaling pathways, respectively. CLEC2B ŌĆōKLRF1 (PIP = 0 .342) implicated AICL (activation-induced C-type lectin, encoded by CLEC2B ) as a ligand for the activating NK receptor NKp80 (encoded by 

KLRF1 ), an axis established to mediate mutual activation between NK cells and myeloid cells 30 , but fell below the discovery threshold. IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .222) fell well short of discovery, confirming that the causal IFN-╬│ signal from CD4 + T cells to NK cells is pri-marily modulated by the expression level of the signal-transducing ╬▓ chain rather than the ligand-binding ╬▒ chain of the receptor complex. 37 0.54 0.62 0.91 0.86

curve crosses zero near +0 .24 standard deviations above the mean PTGER2 level, transi-tioning from suppressive to strongly activating at high EP2 densities. 40 S2.2.4 CD4 + T Cells ŌåÆ Monocytes 

Across 691 donors, MR-CCC evaluated 42 ligandŌĆōreceptorŌĆōpathway triplets for the CD4 + Tcell (sender) to Monocyte (receiver) direction and identified two high-confidence causal com-munication signals with PIP exceeding 0.5: PPBP ŌĆōCXCR2 within the Chemokine signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .988) and ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE5 within the Integrin signaling pathway (PIP = 0 .597) (Figures S22ŌĆōS24). The dominant discovery, PPBP ŌĆōCXCR2 (PIP = 0 .988), identifies the platelet basic protein precursor ( PPBP , which encodes the CXCL7/NAP-2 family of CXC chemokines upon processing) expressed in CD4 + T cells as a causal regulator of monocyte Chemokine pathway activity through the CXC chemokine receptor 2 (CXCR2). CXCL7/NAP-2, the processed product of PPBP, is a potent agonist for CXCR2 on myeloid cells 31 , and CXCR2 is the dominant chemokine receptor governing monocyte recruitment and activation in response to ELR + CXC chemokines. The positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .882) indicates that higher CD4 + Tcell PPBP production exerts a baseline stimulatory effect on monocyte Chemokine pathway activity; however, the interaction term ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ12 .6) is the largest in magnitude of any triplet in the present analysis. The effect curve crosses zero at only ZŌłŚ Ōēł +0 .07 standard deviations above the mean CXCR2 levelŌĆöessentially at the population meanŌĆöand then descends steeply to strongly negative values. Monocytes expressing CXCR2 at or above the population mean therefore experience a rapidly escalating suppression of Chemokine pathway activity as CD4 + T cell PPBP production rises, consistent with receptor saturation and homologous desensitization: CXCR2 is a G protein-coupled receptor subject to rapid phosphorylation, arrestin recruitment, and internalization upon sustained ligand exposure 31 ,and monocytes already expressing high CXCR2 levels may be in a prior state of chemokine exposure that amplifies this counter-regulatory response. The second discovered triplet, ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE5 (PIP = 0 .597), implicates CD4 + T cell 

╬▓1 integrin ( ITGB1 ) as a causal regulator of monocyte Integrin pathway activity through the adhesion G protein-coupled receptor CD97 (encoded by ADGRE5 )24 . The positive main effect ( ╦å╬▓X = 0 .360) and negative interaction ( ╦å╬▓XZ = ŌłÆ0.618) produce a sign-reversing curve that crosses zero approximately 0 .58 standard deviations above the mean ADGRE5 level. 41 Monocytes with low CD97 expression show a modest stimulatory response to CD4 + T cell 

╬▓1 integrin engagement; those expressing ADGRE5 above this threshold transition to a progressively suppressive effect. This pattern contrasts with the same triplet in the CD4 +

T cells ŌåÆ B cells direction, where the interaction term was large and positive ( ╦å╬▓XZ = 3 .63), yielding a monotonically and steeply activating curve. The cell-type-specific sign reversal of the ADGRE5 interaction term between monocytes and B cells reflects the fundamentally different downstream signaling environments of CD97-expressing cells in these two lineages, and illustrates the receiver-cell specificity of MR-CCC discoveries. Notably, several triplets did not reach the discovery threshold. ITGAV ŌĆōADGRE2 (PIP = 0 .484) was the highest-ranking non-discovered triplet and a close near-miss; the same receptor ADGRE2 was part of the top-ranked discovery in the CD4 + T cells ŌåÆ NK cells direction ( ITGB1 ŌĆōADGRE2 , PIP = 0 .910), but here it falls just below threshold, suggesting the EMR2ŌĆōintegrin axis on monocytes may be more heterogeneous at the population level. 

IL1B ŌĆōIL1RAP (PIP = 0 .349) was also a notable near-miss, consistent with the sub-threshold IL-1 ╬▓ signal observed in the CD4 + T cells ŌåÆ NK cells direction as well 29 . IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 

(PIP = 0 .309) and IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR1 (PIP = 0 .159) both fell well below the discovery thresh-old; while CD4 + Th1 cells are a physiological source of IFN-╬│, the IFN-╬│ signal to monocytes does not achieve discovery strength here, in contrast to the CD4 + T cells ŌåÆ NK cells direc-tion where IFNG ŌĆōIFNGR2 was discovered (PIP = 0 .542), suggesting NK cells are a more consistent causal target of Th1-derived IFN-╬│ in this cohort 10 .42 0.99 0.60
